Stewart Shapiroโs [3mThinking about Mathematics [0m(Oxford University Press, 2000) provides an accessible introduction to the Platonic 
view of mathematical objects, as well as to a variety of other theories of the nature of mathematics. 

For a popular yet comprehensive account of theories that conceive of the physical world as the output of a computational process, 
see Kevin Kellyโs โGod Is the Machineโ, [3mWired, [0m10(12) (2002). 

For Bohrโs view of the non-existence of quantum objects, see the discussion in Max Jammerโs [3mThe Philosophy of Quantum Mechanics [0m
(Wiley, 1974), pp. 203โ11. This is an excellent if demanding resource for analyses of the key aspects of the interpretation of the 
quantum mechanical formalism.

The curious experiences of the woman who irretrievably lost her self are described in Suzanne Segalโs very readable memoir [3m

see chapter 8 of David Enoch and Adrian Ball, [3mUncommon Psychiatric Syndromes [0m(Hodder & Stoughton, 2001). 

For an overview of the different locations of the self throughout history, see Giuseppe Santoro et al., โThe Anatomic Location of 
the Soul From the Heart, Through the Brain, To the Whole Body, and Beyondโ, [3mNeurosurgery, [0m65(4) (2009): 633โ43. 

Daniel Dennettโs โWhere Am I?โ is reprinted in chapter 13 of the excellent anthology [3mThe Mindโs I, [0medited by Douglas Hofstadter 
and Daniel Dennett (Harvester Press, 1981). The selection given here is on pp. 218-19. In 1988, the Dutch director Piet Hoenderdos

The experiment with the virtual full-body illusion is described in Thomas Metzingerโs [3mThe Ego Tunnel: The Science of the Mind and

A variant of the thought experiment of the self-destroying drug is described in Raymond Smullyanโs essay โAn Unfortunate Dualistโ 
in his [3mThis Book Needs No Title [0m(Simon & Schuster, 1980), pp. 53โ5. This piece is discussed in [3mThe Mindโs I, [0mpp. 384โ8, where the 
original essay is also reprinted. 

The quote from David Hume comes from his [3mTreatise of Human Nature [0m(Clarendon Press, 1896), p. 252. 

The quote from Descartes can be found in John Cottingham et al., [3mThe Philosophical Writings of Descartes, [0mVol. III: [3mThe 
Correspondence [0m(Cambridge University Press, 1991), p. 143. 

For more on the total flight simulator, see Thomas Metzingerโs [3mThe Ego Tunnel: The Science of the Mind and the Myth of the Self [0m
(Basic Books, 2009), pp. 104โ8. 

For the text of the entire [3mMahapunnama Sutta [0m, see Bikkhu Nanamoli and Bikkhu Bodhi (tr.), [3mThe Middle Length Discourses of the 
Buddha [0m(Wisdom, 1995), pp. 887โ91. For a related view of the self, see Derek Parfitโs [3mReasons and Persons [0m(Clarendon Press, 1984). 

Jorge Luis Borges describes the work of Tsuโi Pen in his story โThe Garden of Forking Pathsโ. See his [3mCollected Fictions [0m(Penguin, 
1999), pp. 119โ28. 

Accessible introductions to the many worlds interpretation are in Nick Herbertโs [3mQuantum Reality [0m(Doubleday, 1985), pp. 172โ5, and 
Paul Daviesโs [3mOther Worlds [0m(Simon & Schuster, 1980). For an interesting discussion that seeks to dispel some of the philosophical

For Libetโs experiments, see Benjamin Libet et al., โTime of Conscious Intention to Act in Relation to Onset of Cerebral Activity

The experiment with the shared computer mouse is described in Daniel Wegner and Thalia Wheatley, โApparent Mental Causation:

Memetics was introduced by Richard Dawkins in his 1976 book [3mThe Selfish Gene [0m, which popularized the idea of gene-centred (rather 
than organism-centred) evolution. For more information on the t-gene in mice, see p. 236 of the thirtieth anniversary edition 
(Oxford, 2006). The view of the relation between memes and the self is set forth in Daniel Dennettโs [3mConsciousness Explained [0m
(Penguin, 1993), pp. 199โ208. A book-length discussion arriving at similar conclusions is Susan Blackmoreโs [3mThe Meme Machine [0m
(Oxford University Press, 1999). For a different interpretation, see Kate Distinโs [3mThe Selfish Meme: A Critical Reassessment [0m
(Cambridge University Press, 2005).

The legend of the monk of Heisterbach is told in Goswin Peter Rathโs [3mRheinische Legenden [0m(Greven Verlag Cologne, 1955), pp. 
178โ81. 

McTaggart describes his proof of the unreality of time first in a paper of the same title in volume 17 of [3mMind [0m(1908: 457โ74), and 
later in chapter 33 of his two-volume [3mThe Nature of Existence [0m(Cambridge University Press, 1921). An accessible summary of the 
argument can be found in chapter 8 of Robin Le Poidevinโs [3mTravels in Four Dimensions: The Enigmas of Space and Time [0m(Oxford 
University Press, 2003). McTaggartโs argument has triggered a large amount of philosophical discussion; the Further Reading in 
this volume lists the most important contributions. 

A clear discussion of Gรถdelโs thought on time can be found in Palle Yourgrauโs [3mGรถdel Meets Einstein [0m(Open Court, 1999). For an 
excellent explanation of the relativity of simultaneity, see Martin Gardnerโs [3mRelativity for the Million [0m(Macmillan, 1962), pp. 
40โ5. 

Russellโs five-minute hypothesis comes from his [3mThe Analysis of Mind [0m(Allen & Unwin, 1921), p. 159. A similar argument is used by 
creationists to explain the existence of objects apparently pre-dating their preferred date of creation: God, it is claimed, just 
created all the apparent records of an illusory past at the same time as everything else. For some discussion, see chapter 1 of 
Martin Gardnerโs [3mDid Adam and Eve Have Navels? [0m(W. W. Norton, 2000). 

Felix Eberty first describes his idea of the present universe as a massive visual archive of the past in a short anonymous 
pamphlet [3mDie Gestirne und die Weltgeschichte; Gedanken รผber Raum, Zeit und Ewigkeit [0mpublished in 1846. It was further developed by 
Harry Mulisch in his 1997 novel [3mThe Discovery of Heaven [0m: โIf we had the technology to place a mirror on a celestial object forty 
light-years away, beamed images from earth to that mirror, then gazed at it through a very powerful telescope, we would see right 
now reflections of what took place on earth eighty years ago โ forty years for earthโs light to reach the distant planet, and 
forty years for the reflection to reach earth. Past and present merge.โ 

On the phantom time hypothesis, see Heribert Illig, [3mDas erfundene Mittelalter. Die grรถรte Zeitfรคlschung der Geschichte [0m(Econ, 
1996). Material in English is limited, a summary can be found in Hans-Ulrich Niemitzโs โDid the Early Middle Ages Really Exist?โ, 
at http://www.cl.cam.ac.uk/~mgk25/volatile/Niemitz-1997.pdf. For a brief discussion, see also John Grantโs [3mBogus Science [0m(Wisley, 
2009), pp. 179โ85. 

For an accessible summary of the delayed-choice experiment, see Nick Herbertโs [3mQuantum Reality [0m(Doubleday, 1985), pp. 164โ8. You 
can do your own delayed-choice experiment at home by following the description in Rachel Hillmer and Paul Kwiat, โA Do-It-Yourself 
Quantum Eraserโ, [3mScientific American [0m(May 2007): 90โ5. 

The name โAndromeda paradoxโ derives from the discussion by Roger Penrose in his [3mThe Emperorโs New Mind [0m(Oxford University Press, 
1999), pp. 260-1. The paradox had previously been discovered independently by C. W. Rietdijk in โA Rigorous Proof of Determinism 
Derived from the Special Theory of Relativityโ, [3mPhilosophy of Science, [0m33 (1966): 341โ4, and by Hilary Putnam in โTime and 
Physical Geometryโ, [3mJournal of Philosophy, [0m64 (1967): 240โ4. For a detailed analysis of this paradox, see section 3 of the entry 
โBeing and Becoming in Modern Physicsโ in the [3mStanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy [0mat http://plato.stanford.edu/entries/ 
spacetime-bebecome. 

The extract from the [3mConfessions [0mof St Augustine comes from section 26 of the eleventh book, E. B. Pusey (tr.), [3mThe Confessions of 
S. Augustine [0m(John Henry Parker, 1838), p. 239. 

For research into the duration of the subjective present, see Ernst Pรถppel, [3mMindworks: Time and Conscious Experience [0m(Harcourt 
Brace Jovanovich, 1988). 

For some discussion of how the brain represents time, see pp. 144โ53 of Daniel Dennettโs [3mConsciousness Explained [0m(Penguin, 1991). 

A description of Libetโs experiments aimed at a general readership can be found in chapter 2 of his [3mMind Time: The Temporal Factor

The โtimelessโ theory described at the end of the chapter is due to Julian Barbour and is explained in detail in his book [3mThe End
